23
Various Gods (Va╠Дyu 1, Indra and Va╠Дyu 2тАУ3, Mitra and Varun╠гa 4тАУ6, Indra Marutvant 7тАУ9, All Gods 10тАУ12, Pu╠Дsan 13тАУ15, Waters ╠г 16тАУ23ab, Agni 23cdтАУ24)
Medh─Бtithi K─Бс╣Зva
24 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except pura├╝с╣гс╣Зih 19, anuс╣гс╣нubh 20, 22тАУ24, pratiс╣гс╣нh─Б 21, arranged in tr╠еcas
Although the principles of hymn arrangement strongly suggest that this twenty four-verse hymn is a composite, consisting of eight individual tr╠еcas, the situation is quite different from the previous hymn, I.22, where the collection was dictated merely and mechanically by the number of verses in each segment, without a par ticular ritual application. Here the separate tr╠еcas follow the order of a structured recitation in the Morning Pressing, later called the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra. Other instances of this litany are found in R╠еgveda I.2тАУ3 and II.41, and to some extent I.139; for a detailed discussion of the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra see the introduction to I.2.
This hymn varies somewhat from the standard Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra, which has the fol lowing divinities in the following order: V─Бyu (1), Indra-V─Бyu (2), Mitra-Varuс╣Зa (3), A┼Ыvins (4), Indra (5), the All Gods (6), Sarasvat─л (7). This hymn lacks the A┼Ыvins in position 4, but in position 5 Indra, instead of being alone, is accompanied by the Maruts, and though the following tr╠еca (vss. 10тАУ12) is ascribed by the Anukramaс╣З─л to the All Gods, it is dominated by the Maruts. Since offering to Indra with the Maruts is made only in the Midday Pressing, and to the A┼Ыvins in the Morning Pressing, perhaps this version of the litany is shifting its focus to the Midday Pressing and to the ritual innovation that extended offering to the Maruts, rather than just Indra, at that pressing. (See further discussion in the introduction to I.165.) P┼лс╣гan is also added after the All Gods (position 6), and instead of the divine river Sarasvat─л in position 7 we find the functionally similar Waters.
The first three verses to the waters (16тАУ18) bring the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra proper to an end. The last six verses (19тАУ24) are a supplement, in a somewhat Atharvan style, treating the waters as healers and removers of transgressions. These functions of the waters bring to mind the тАЬFinal BathтАЭ or avabhr╠еtha in classical ┼Ыrauta ritual, in which the sacrificer and his wife wash each other at the conclusion of the sacri
fice, and these verses may have been included in this hymn in order to encompass the entire soma-pressing day, from the first offering to V─Бyu to the final cleansing. The middle four verses of this sequence (20тАУ23) are also found in a hymn to the waters, X.9.6тАУ9, and the introductory and final verses here (19 and 24) may have been added to create two triplets for this tr╠еca hymn.
As in other of Medh─БtithiтАЩs hymns, the actual contents are fairly simplistic, consisting primarily of invocations to the various gods and invitations to the soma-drinking. Perhaps the most interesting sequence is the tr╠еca to P┼лс╣гan (vss. 13тАУ15), who finds the hidden king and is urged to drive him here тАЬlike lost live
stock.тАЭ Most commentators identify this king as Soma, but the thematics and phraseologyтАФparticularly the notion of finding and returning a hidden deityтАФare much more characteristic of Agni, and we have interpreted these verses in that way. Whether the king is Agni or Soma, however, it is not clear what this snatch of myth is doing here in this hymn, though P┼лс╣гanтАЩs ability to locate lost cows is proverbial.

Various gods (Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra) I.23.4-6: This tс╣Ыca to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa stations the two names in three different ways in the three verses. +Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI invoke Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, who with true speech, are the encouragers of pious acts, and are lords of true lighс╣нтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mitra and Varuс╣Зa are among the eights sons of Aditi, ─Аdityas]. [с╣Ыtasya jyotiс╣гas-pati: ┼Ыrutyantare c─Бс╣гс╣нau putr─Бso aditeс╕е ityupakramya mitra┼Ыca varuс╣Зa┼Ыca ity─Бdikam ─Бmn─Бtam (Taittir─лya ─Аraс╣Зyaka 1.13.2-3)

+Jamison Brereton

Those who through truth increase by truth, the lords of truth, of light, these two, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, do I call.

+Griffith

Those who by Law uphold the Law, Lords of the shining light of Law,
Mitra I call, and Varuna.

+Geldner

Die durch die Wahrheit Wahrheitsmehrer sind, die Herren der Wahrheit, des Lichts, Mitra und Varuna, diese beiden rufe ich.

+Grassmann

Die sich durch Recht des Rechtes freun, des Rechtes und des Glanzes Herrn, Mitra ruf’ ich und Varuna.

+Elizarenkova

тАЬWe invoke Indra, attended by the Maruts to drink the Soma juice; may he, with his associates, be satisfied.тАЭ

We call Indra accompanied by the Maruts here for soma-drinking. Along with the troop let him reach satiety.

Indra, by Maruts girt, we call to drink the Soma juice: may he
Sate him in union with his troop.

+Grassmann

+Jamison Brereton

Having Indra as chief, the Maruts as troop, and the gifts of P┼лс╣гan, o gods,
all of you, hear my call.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is striking that all of ab is made up of vocatives, with each one accented: because of the place of the accent, three of the four words have to be vocatives; only ├нndrajyeс╣гс╣нh─Б(h) could be nom. pl., since ├нndra- has inherent initial accent. The first word of c, v├н┼Ыve, may also be and probably is a voc., making a pair with voc. d├йv─Бsaс╕е, which opens the preceding p─Бda. On the voc. of v├н┼Ыva- see comm. ad X.15.6.

It would be satisfying to have three GOD-X bahuvr─лhis parallel in semantic and morphological structure, but although Geldner (followed by Witzel Got┼Н) interprets the r─Бti- in p┼л╠Бс╣гa-r─Бtayaс╕е as an agent noun (тАЬmit P┼лс╣гan als G├╢nnerтАЭ), r─Бt├н- both as simplex and in its fairly numerous compounds is always an abstract тАШgivingтАЩ or concretized version thereof (тАШgiftтАЩ), as its morphology as a deverbal feminine abstract would require. I therefore take the third cmpd as a tatpuruс╣гa p┼лс╣гa-r─Бt├н- the gift(s)/giving of P┼лс╣гanтАЩ. It owes its initial accent to the fact that it is a voc. (as does the bahuvr─лhi m├бrudgaс╣З─Бс╕е [expect *mar├║dgaс╣Зa-].) The тАШgiftтАЩ or тАШgivingтАЩ of P┼лс╣гan is described as auspicious (bhadr─Б╠Б) in VI.58.1.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (Witzel Got┼Н), following Grassmann, tr. s├бhas─Б as an adj. modifying Indra (тАЬmit dem starken IndraтАЭ), but this is of course impossible. With that accent it must be a neut.; accent shift to *sah├бs- would turn it into an adjective, but this form is unattested (versus, e.g., y├б┼Ыas- тАШgloryтАЩ├а ya┼Ы├бs- тАШgloriousтАЩ).

On the analysis of fairly common 3rd sg. ─л┼Ыata (always with m─Б╠Б(kiс╕е)) as an injunc. to a reduplicated aor., see Hoffmann 1967 (Injunk.): 64-66 (seemingly accepted by Lubotsky, Concordance). Although he adduces semantic and syntactic factors that impose this interpretation, it nonetheless does not seem entirely satisfying, because the thematic stem envisioned (─л┼Ыa- [never accented]) seems insufficiently distinguished from the presential perfect stem ─л╠Б┼Ы-, and Hoffmann does not suggest a mechanism for deriving such an aorist stem from either the presential perfect stem or directly from the root. Moreover, his argument that m─Б╠Бpreventive clauses should have an aorist might falter in the face of a root that simply lacks an aorist. (See now Ian HollenbaughтАЩs work demonstrating just that.) I prefer DebrunnerтАЩs explanation, rejected by Hoffmann, that ─л┼Ыata represents a re-marking of ─л┼Ыa with -ta to make it more clearly a 3rd sg. Judging from the accent (─л╠Б┼Ыe, ─л╠Б┼Ы─Бna- [versus ─л┼Ы─Бn├б-]), the old presential perfect had been mostly reanalyzed as a root present, and ─л┼Ыa would be an anomalous 3rd sg.

injunctive to such a present.

I.23.13-15: As noted in the introduction, I take the тАЬkingтАЭ that P┼лс╣гan is returning as Agni, not, with most tr., Soma. The theme of the finding and returning of the god-in-hiding in 14 is much more appropriate for Agni than for Soma, and the тАЬglitttering barhisтАЭ is also more likely to be associated with Agni. Both Agni and Soma are called тАЬbuttress, supportтАЭ (13) (Agni in V.15.1-2) and both are called king (14). The drops (├нndu-) in 15 might seem rather to indicate Soma, but in VI.16.16 Agni is strengthened by drops (├нndubhiс╕е), which must be drops of ghee.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬVerily he has brought to me successively the six (seasons), connected with the drops (of the Soma juice) as (a husbandsman) repeatedly plural ughs (the earth) for barley.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъat. = vasant─Бdin с╣Ыtun, the spring and the rest of seasons

+Jamison Brereton

And with drops (of ghee) he will keep driving along to me the six yoked (flames),
as if plowing a grain(field) with oxen.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The ritual referent of the тАЬsix yokedтАЭ entities (с╣г├бс╕Н yukt─Б╠Бn) is unclear, no matter whether Soma or Agni is taken as the main referent: those in the Soma camp consider the yoked ones to be the dakс╣гiс╣З─Бs due the poet; I consider them the flames of the recovered Agni, roused by the drops of ghee. In terms of the simile in c, the six yoked ones are clearly the teams for plowing. See esp. AV VI.91.1, cited by Schaefer (1994: 197). On anu тИЪsidh as тАШentlangtreibenтАЩ, see Schaefer 1994: 196-97.

In my translation I have reversed the renderings of the finite intensive (unaccented carkс╣Ы┼Ыat in c) and the intensive participle (accented anus├йс╣гidhat) to make the relationship between simile and frame clearer.

+Griffith

And may he. duly bring to me the six bound closely, through these drops,
As one who ploughs with steers brings corn.

mixing the milk with honey.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAmbrosia is in the waters; in the waters are medicinal herbs; therefore, divine (priest), be prompt in their praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Deva = с╣Ыtvij and other br─Бhmaс╣Зas; ete vai dev─Бс╕е pratyakс╣гam yad br─Бhmaс╣З─Бс╕е = these dieties, who are perceptibly (present) are the br─Бhmaс╣Зas (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.7.3.1)

+Jamison Brereton

Within the waters is deathlessness, in the waters healing, and (it is right) to glorify the waters.
O gods, become prizewinners.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Again I disagree with most tr. in the disposition of the b p─Бda. I take it with a, because I think we mortals are to glorify the waters. Others think the gods should become strong or victorious in order to praise the waters - but gods are not usually the agents of such praising.

I.23.20-23 = X.9.6-9, save that the fourth p─Бda of 20 is missing in X.9.6.

+Griffith

Amrit is in the Waters in the Waters there is healing balm
Be swift, ye Gods, to give them praise.

+Geldner

In den Gew├дssern ist Lebensbalsam, in den Gew├дssern Arzenei, und zu Ehren der Gew├дsser seid, ihr G├╢tter, siegesstark!

+Grassmann

Im Wasser ist Ambrosia und Arzenei; die Wasser zu verherrlichen, Seid, o ihr G├╢tter, schnell zur Hand.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSoma has declared to me, ‘all medicaments, as well as Agni, the benefactor of the universe, are in the waters’; the waters, contain all healing herbs.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Entrance of Agni into the water is noted in many plural ces: so ─Бpaс╕е pr─Бvi┼Ыat (Taittir─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 2.6.6.1);

Legend: Agni hides himself through fear, an allusion to subservience of waters to Agni

+Jamison Brereton

тАЬWithin the waters,тАЭ Soma said to me, тАЬare all healing remedies, and Agni who is weal to all.тАЭ And the waters are healing for all.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The semi-direct speech and esp. the casual conversational tone of this verse are quite unusual for the RV. Although most tr. take the whole as indirect speech (тАЬSoma said to me thatтАжтАЭ), the construction of the verse seems to me to mix direct and indirect speech, with c, couched in the acc., shading into indirect speech. I take the final p─Бda separately, as it is absent from the parallel in X.9.6.

Note the distraction of the aps├║ ant├бr phrase that opens 19a into two p─Бda opening words: 20a #aps├║ тАж b #ant├бr.

+Griffith

Within the Waters–Soma thus hath told me–dwell all balms that heal,
And Agni, he who blesseth all. The Waters hold all medicines.

+Geldner

Soma belehrt mich, da├Я in den Wassern alle Arzeneien und der allersprie├Яliche Agni sei, und da├Я die Wasser allheilend sind.

+Grassmann

Im Wasser, sagte Soma mir, ist alle Arzenei vereint Und Agni, der das All erquickt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWaters, take away whatever sin has been (found) in me whether I have (knowingly) done wrong, or have pronounced imprecations (against holy men) or (have spoken) untruth.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Waters, carry this away, whatever trouble is in meтАФ
whether I have committed deceit or I have cursedтАФas well as untruth.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The construction of the 2nd hemistich is complex, containing a double v─Б conjoining two y├бd clauses and an ut├б, which reaches back to conjoin the indefinite y├бt k├нm ca durit├бm mama тАЬwhatever trouble is in meтАЭ (b) and the final word of the vs. ├бnс╣Ыtam (d). The two y├бd clauses of cd are alternative expansions of the indefinite expression of b, while ├бnс╣Ыtam is a new term. So Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н, and, with explicit disc. of the construction, Klein (DGRV I.301). By contrast L├╝ders (417; sim. Ober II.37) takes ├бnс╣Ыtam as part of the 2nd y├бd v─Б clause and seems to ignore the ut├б: тАЬтАж was immer Sunde an mir ist, was ich betrogen habe oder was ich geschworen habe als L├╝ge

+Griffith

Whatever sin is found in me, whatever evil I have wrought.
If I have lied or falsely sworn, Waters, remove it far from me.

+Geldner

Ihr Gew├дsser f├╝hret all das fort, was von Fehle an mir ist, sei es da├Я ich treulos war, oder da├Я ich geflucht habe und jede Unwahrheit!

+Grassmann

O Wasser, traget alles fort, was irgend Unrecht ist an mir, Was andern Uebles ich gethan, was ich gelogen, was geflucht.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI have this day entered into the waters; we have mingled with their essence; Agni, abiding in the waters, approach, and fill me, thus (bathed), with vigour.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rasena samagasmahi: we have become associated with the essence of water, jalasareс╣Зa saс╣Еgat─Бс╕е smaс╕е).

+Jamison Brereton

O Waters, today I have followed (you). We have united with your sap. Full of milk, come here, o Agni. Merge me with luster.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Most tr. take ─Б╠Бpaс╕е as acc. here (тАЬI have followed the waters.тАЭ). This is of course possible: the nom. of this stem does get used for acc. occasionally in the RV.

However, such an interpr. is not nec. in this case, since it is easy to supply an acc. тАЬyou.тАЭ And the fact that the two previous vss. (21a and 22a) contain vocatives ─Б╠Бpaс╕е and ─Бpaс╕е respectively supports a vocative interpretation here.

+Griffith

The Waters I this day have sought, and to their moisture have we come:
O Agni, rich in milk, come thou, and with thy splendour cover me.

+Geldner

Die Gew├дsser habe ich heut aufgesucht; wir sind mit dem Na├Я in Ber├╝hrung gekommen. Komm Milch bringend, Agni; begabe mich hier mit Ansehen!

+Grassmann

Den Wassern ging ich heute nach, wir einten uns mit ihrer Flut; Komm, Agni, her mit Milch benetzt, und mich benetze du mit Glanz.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAgni, confer upon me vigour, progeny and life, so that the gods may know the (sacrifice) of this my (employer), and Indra with the с╣Ъс╣гis, may know it.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Merge me with luster, Agni, with offspring, with long life.
The gods should know this (hymn?) of mine; Indra should know it
along with the seers.
As Oldenberg (1888: 225) observes, I.24тАУ30, the ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa hymns, like the preced ing Medh─Бtithi hymns (I 12тАУ23), generally follow the organization of the hymns of Maс╣Зс╕Нala VIII. He argues that irregularities in the placement of I.25, 27, and 30 can be explained if these hymns are composites of several hymns.
The story of ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa, the putative poet of these hymns, appears in Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa VII 13тАУ18 and ┼Ъ─Бс╣Еkh─Бyana ┼Ъrauta S┼лtra XV 17тАУ27. According to the story, King Hari┼Ыcandra had begged Varuс╣Зa for a son and promised that if Varuс╣Зa gave him one, he would sacrifice his son to the god. A boy, Rohita, was born to Hari┼Ыcandra, but the king managed to delay the sacrifice of his son until Rohita reached adulthood. When the king could no longer avoid the inevitable sacrifice, he told Rohita that he was to be sacrificed to Varuс╣Зa. But Rohita refused to be the sacrificial victim and departed the kingdom. As a result Hari┼Ыcandra was struck by dropsy in punishment for not performing the sacrifice.
In his travels Rohita eventually came upon a poor brahmin named Aj─лgarta, who sold his son ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa to Rohita to be a substitute sacrificial victim. Rohita returned with ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa and Varuс╣Зa accepted the substitution of ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa for Rohita. But when ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa was bound to the stake and was about to be killed, he appealed to the gods by reciting I.24.1 to Praj─Бpati, the god Ka (cf. 1a ka╠Бsya тАЬof which (god)?тАЭ and 1c ka╠Бс╕е тАЬwho?тАЭ), 24.2 to Agni, 24.3тАУ5 to Savitar, 24.6тАУ15 and I.25 to Varuс╣Зa, I.26 and 27.1тАУ12 to Agni, 27.13 to the All Gods, I.29 and 30.1тАУ16 to Indra, 30.17тАУ19 to the A┼Ыvins, and 30.20тАУ22 to Dawn. Each time ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa recited a verse, one of his bonds was loosened and Hari┼ЫcandraтАЩs belly became smaller. With the last verse ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa was free of his bonds and Hari┼Ыcandra was free of disease. Although I.24 refers directly to ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa and to his rescue by Varuс╣Зa, the story of ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa in the form in which it told in the Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa does not fully correspond to that at the basis of any of the hymns in this collection. Probably closer to the R╠еgvedic version is that alluded to in the Yajurveda. Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б
V 2.1.3 and K─Бс╣нhaka Saс╣Гhit─Б XIX 11 say simply that ┼Ъunaс╕е┼Ыepa had been seized by Varuс╣Зa but then rescued himself from Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs bonds.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is difficult to know what, if anything, is the referent of asya. I have tentatively supplied тАШhymnтАЩ, but the poet may simply be calling upon the gods to witness the general situation (so Geldner). The same expression тИЪVID me asya is found in the refrain of I.105, except with accented asy├б, for which reason I more confidently supply тАШspeechтАЩ there.

[I.24-25 JPB]
